height: 0em;"></span><span class="MJXp-msup" id="MJXp-Span-65"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-66" style="margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="MJXp-mi" id="MJXp-Span-67">e</span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow MJXp-script" id="MJXp-Span-68" style="vertical-align: 0.5em;"><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-69">−</span><span class="MJXp-mn" id="MJXp-Span-70">1</span></span></span><span class="MJXp-mspace" id="MJXp-Span-71" style="width: 0.25em; height: 0em;"></span><span class="MJXp-msub" id="MJXp-Span-72"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-73" style="margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="MJXp-mi" id="MJXp-Span-74">Na</span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow MJXp-script" id="MJXp-Span-75" style="vertical-align: -0.4em;"><span class="MJXp-mn" id="MJXp-Span-76">3</span></span></span><span class="MJXp-mi" id="MJXp-Span-77">Sb</span><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-78" style="margin-left: 0.111em; margin-right: 0.111em;">/</span><span class="MJXp-mi" id="MJXp-Span-79">P</span></span></span></span></span></span><script type="math/mml" id="MathJax-Element-2"><math display="block" indentalign="left"><mrow><mrow><mstyle indentshift="3em" indentshiftlast="3em"><msub><mrow><mi>Na</mi></mrow><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">x</mi></mrow></msub><mi>Sb</mi><mo>/</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">P</mi><mo>+</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mn>3</mn><mo>−</mo><mi>x</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mspace width="0.25em"></mspace><msup><mrow><mi>Na</mi></mrow><mrow><mo>+</mo></mrow></msup><mo>+</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mn>3</mn><mo>−</mo><mi>x</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mspace width="0.25em"></mspace><msup><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">e</mi></mrow><mrow><mo>−</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></msup><mspace width="0.25em"></mspace><msub><mrow><mi>Na</mi></mrow><mrow><mn>3</mn></mrow></msub><mi>Sb</mi><mo>/</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">P</mi></mstyle></mrow></mrow></math></script></div><div class="label"><span class="labelSpan">(2)</span></div></div><div class="MathJaxEquation" id="eq3"><div class="equation"><span class="MathJax_Preview" style="color: inherit;"><span class="MJXp-math MJXp-display" id="MJXp-Span-80"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-81"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-82"><span class="MJXp-mstyle" id="MJXp-Span-83"><span class="MJXp-msub" id="MJXp-Span-84"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-85" style="margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="MJXp-mi" id="MJXp-Span-86">Na</span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow MJXp-script" id="MJXp-Span-87" style="vertical-align: -0.4em;"><span class="MJXp-mn" id="MJXp-Span-88">3</span></span></span><span class="MJXp-mi" id="MJXp-Span-89">Sb</span><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-90" style="margin-left: 0.111em; margin-right: 0.111em;">/</span><span class="MJXp-mi" id="MJXp-Span-91">P</span><span class="MJXp-mspace" id="MJXp-Span-92" style="width: 0.25em; height: 0em;"></span><span class="MJXp-mi" id="MJXp-Span-93">NaP</span><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-94" style="margin-left: 0.111em; margin-right: 0.111em;">/</span><span class="MJXp-mi" id="MJXp-Span-95">Sb</span><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-96" style="margin-left: 0.267em; margin-right: 0.267em;">+</span><span class="MJXp-msub" id="MJXp-Span-97"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-98" style="margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="MJXp-mi" id="MJXp-Span-99">Na</span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow MJXp-script" id="MJXp-Span-100" style="vertical-align: -0.4em;"><span class="MJXp-mn" id="MJXp-Span-101">2</span></span></span><span class="MJXp-mi" id="MJXp-Span-102">P</span><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-103" style="margin-left: 0.111em; margin-right: 0.111em;">/</span><span class="MJXp-mi" id="MJXp-Span-104">Sb</span><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-105" style="margin-left: 0.267em; margin-right: 0.267em;">+</span><span class="MJXp-mi" id="MJXp-Span-106">P</span><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-107" style="margin-left: 0.267em; margin-right: 0.267em;">+</span><span class="MJXp-mi" id="MJXp-Span-108">Sb</span><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-109" style="margin-left: 0.267em; margin-right: 0.267em;">+</span><span class="MJXp-msup" id="MJXp-Span-110"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-111" style="margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="MJXp-mi" id="MJXp-Span-112">Na</span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow MJXp-script" id="MJXp-Span-113" style="vertical-align: 0.5em;"><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-114">+</span></span></span><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-115" style="margin-left: 0.267em; margin-right: 0.267em;">+</span><span class="MJXp-msup" id="MJXp-Span-116"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-117" style="margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="MJXp-mi" id="MJXp-Span-118">e</span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow MJXp-script" id="MJXp-Span-119" style="vertical-align: 0.5em;"><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-120">−</span><span class="MJXp-mn" id="MJXp-Span-121">1</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><script type="math/mml" id="MathJax-Element-3"><math display="block" indentalign="left"><mrow><mrow><mstyle indentshift="3em" indentshiftlast="3em"><msub><mrow><mi>Na</mi></mrow><mrow><mn>3</mn></mrow></msub><mi>Sb</mi><mo>/</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">P</mi><mspace width="0.25em"></mspace><mi>NaP</mi><mo>/</mo><mi>Sb</mi><mo>+</mo><msub><mrow><mi>Na</mi></mrow><mrow><mn>2</mn></mrow></msub><mi mathvariant="normal">P</mi><mo>/</mo><mi>Sb</mi><mo>+</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">P</mi><mo>+</mo><mi>Sb</mi><mo>+</mo><msup><mrow><mi>Na</mi></mrow><mrow><mo>+</mo></mrow></msup><mo>+</mo><msup><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">e</mi></mrow><mrow><mo>−</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></msup></mstyle></mrow></mrow></math></script></div><div class="label"><span class="labelSpan">(3)</span></div></div></div><div class="NLM_p">The charging/discharging pattern of the Sb@P-N/C electrode is also provided in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 3</a>b. As shown, the tilt plateaus at ∼0.48 and ∼0.84 V represent the alloying and dealloying processes of Sb and Na, which is also consistent with the CV results stated in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 3</a>a. As seen, the charging/discharging curves of the 2nd cycle to the 100th cycle almost overlap each other, the voltage platform in the charging/discharging curve corresponds exactly to the peak position in the CV curve, and each platform keeps nearly no change in the 200 cycles, which further indicates that the obtained Sb@P-N/C anode exhibits high reversibility and cycling stability. More information about the charging/discharging curves for the Sb@C and Sb@N/C anodes are also displayed in Supporting Information <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.3c03340/suppl_file/am3c03340_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S11</a>. Furthermore, the comparison of the cycle performance of the Sb@C, Sb@N/C, and Sb@P-N/C electrodes measured at 50 mA g<sup>–1</sup> is depicted in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 3</a>c. Distinctly, all compared electrodes show decent cycle stability and capacity retention rate, and the Sb@P-N/C anode displays better specific capacity than the others. Even after 100 cycles, the Sb@P-N/C anode still retains a reversible specific capacity of 525.5 mAh g<sup>–1</sup>, with a retention rate of 95.5%, while the Sb@N/C and Sb@C anodes present capacity and retention ratios of 415.5 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> (94%) and 386.6 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> (88.9%), respectively. In addition, despite the exact cause of why the Coulombic efficiency (CE) of the Sb@P-N/C electrode during subsequent cycling is higher than 100%, it is tentatively explained that the sodium foil of the counter electrode compensates for the loss of sodium metal during cycling, resulting in a higher CE. The better electrochemical property of the Sb@P-N/C can be ascribed to the co-occurrence of P and N elements in the fabricated anodes because P can contribute a certain specific capacity to the electrode and N can provide more active sites for Na<sup>+</sup> ion transfer, except that the hexagonal nano-Sb combined with the carbon fibers do tolerate the volume change in the sodiation/desodiation process and shrink the Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion length as well as increase the ion migration rate. Furthermore, for better comparison, a table about the previously reported data related to Sb-based anode materials is also listed in Supporting Information <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.3c03340/suppl_file/am3c03340_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Table S4</a>.</div><div class="NLM_p"><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 3</a>d exhibits the rate performance comparison of the varied anodes. Obviously, the reversible capacities of the Sb@P-N/C anodes at current densities of 30, 50, 100, 200, and 500 mA g<sup>–1</sup> are 424.9, 410.3, 390.3, 363.9, and 331.8 mAh g<sup>–1</sup>, respectively, while, the Sb@N/C exhibits specific capacities of 392.5, 360.4, 345.6, 323.7, and 308.5 mAh g<sup>–1</sup>, separately, and Sb@C gives an inferior rate capability compared that of the former two at the same current densities. This is mainly owing to the benign linking and contact between the nanocrystals, which facilitates the efficient shift of Na<sup>+</sup> ions from the solvent to the electrode and vice versa. Moreover, <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 3</a>e plots the cycling performance of Sb@P-N/C at varied current densities of 0.5, 1.0, and 5.0 A g<sup>–1</sup>. The initial activation current density of Sb@P-N/C is adapted to 1/10 of testing current and corresponds to 0.05, 0.1 A, and 0.5 A g<sup>–1</sup>, respectively. Obviously, as the current density increases, the specific capacity is clearly decreased; after 400 cycles, the capacity retention rate reached ∼90% compared to the original 10th capacity. More information about the cycling performance analysis of Sb@C and Sb@N/C is exhibited in Supporting Information <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.3c03340/suppl_file/am3c03340_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S12</a>. Moreover, the rate performance of the three compared samples at high current densities is also shown in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.3c03340/suppl_file/am3c03340_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S12</a>.</div><div class="NLM_p">In order to further reveal the reaction kinetics of the fabricated electrodes of Sb@C, Sb@N/C, and Sb@P-N/C, the Nyquist plots of electrochemical impedance spectroscopy (EIS) is plotted in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 4</a>a, and the fitting analysis is given in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 4</a>b. Typically, the EIS is composed of semi-circular arcs in the high-frequency zone and slanted lines in the low-frequency zone.</div><figure id="fig4" data-index="4" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 4</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.3c03340/asset/images/medium/am3c03340_0005.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.3c03340/asset/images/large/am3c03340_0005.jpeg" id="gr4" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 4. (a) EIS plots of the Sb@C, Sb@N/C and Sb@P-N/C electrodes; (b) relation between <i>Z</i><sub>re</sub> and ω<sup>–1/2</sup> in the low-frequency zone; (c-e) CV curves of the samples at different scan rates from 0.1 to 0.5 mV s<sup>–1</sup>; (f) correlation between the peak current and sample scanning rate.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.3c03340/asset/images/large/am3c03340_0005.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.3c03340&amp;id=fig4"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">Generally, it is believed that the sloping lines in the low-frequency zone reflect Na<sup>+</sup> ion diffusion resistance, whereas the semi-circular arcs in the mid–high-frequency zone reveal the resistance of the solid inter-electrolyte (<i>R</i><sub>SEI</sub>) and charge transfer impedance (<i>R</i><sub>ct</sub>). The inset in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 4</a>a is the equivalent circuit for the simulated EIS, where <i>R</i><sub>elect</sub> stands for electrical contact resistance, <i>Q</i> represents the capacitance associated with the SEI membrane, <i>C</i> refers to the capacitance associated with the charge transfer, and <i>W</i><sub>0</sub> is the Warburg impedance associated with the Na<sup>+</sup> ion diffusion. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref47 ref56 ref57 ref58" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref47 ref56 ref57 ref58" aria-label="reference 47 and 56 to 58">(47,56−58)</a> As depicted in the plotting, the charge transfer resistance of Sb@P-N/C, 78.3 Ω, is smaller than that of Sb@C, 138.1 Ω, and Sb@N/C, 104.5 Ω. It is further indicated that the addition of elemental P and N can decrease the transfer resistance, resulting in the improved diffusion kinetics. Additionally, the real part impedance <i>Z</i><sub>re</sub> versus frequency ω<sup>–1/2</sup> graphs is also plotted by fitting a slant straight line in the frequency range of 0.1–1.0 Hz according to <a class="ref internalNav" href="#eq4" aria-label="eq 4">eq 4</a> as follows: <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref59 ref62" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref59 ref62" aria-label="reference 59 and 62">(59,62)</a><div class="MathJaxEquation" id="eq4"><div class="equation"><span class="MathJax_Preview" style="color: inherit;"><span class="MJXp-math MJXp-display" id="MJXp-Span-122"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-123"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-124"><span class="MJXp-mstyle" id="MJXp-Span-125"><span class="MJXp-msub" id="MJXp-Span-126"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-127" style="margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-128">Z</span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow MJXp-script" id="MJXp-Span-129" style="vertical-align: -0.4em;"><span class="MJXp-mi" id="MJXp-Span-130">re</span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-131"><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-132" style="margin-left: 0.333em; margin-right: 0.333em;">=</span><span class="MJXp-mstyle" id="MJXp-Span-133"><span class="MJXp-msub" id="MJXp-Span-134"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-135" style="margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-136">R</span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow MJXp-script" id="MJXp-Span-137" style="vertical-align: -0.4em;"><span class="MJXp-mi" id="MJXp-Span-138">s</span></span></span><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-139" style="margin-left: 0.267em; margin-right: 0.267em;">+</span><span class="MJXp-msub" id="MJXp-Span-140"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-141" style="margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-142">R</span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow MJXp-script" id="MJXp-Span-143" style="vertical-align: -0.4em;"><span class="MJXp-mi" id="MJXp-Span-144">ct</span></span></span><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-145" style="margin-left: 0.267em; margin-right: 0.267em;">+</span><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-146">k</span><span class="MJXp-msup" id="MJXp-Span-147"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-148" style="margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-149">ω</span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow MJXp-script" id="MJXp-Span-150" style="vertical-align: 0.5em;"><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-151">−</span><span class="MJXp-mn" id="MJXp-Span-152">1</span><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-153">/</span><span class="MJXp-mn" id="MJXp-Span-154">2</span></span></span></span></span></span></span><script type="math/mml" id="MathJax-Element-4"><math display="block" indentalign="left"><mrow><mrow><mstyle indentshift="3em" indentshiftlast="3em"><msub><mrow><mi>Z</mi></mrow><mrow><mi>re</mi></mrow></msub></mstyle></mrow></mrow><mrow><mo linebreak="nobreak">=</mo><mstyle indentshift="3em" indentshiftlast="3em"><msub><mrow><mi>R</mi></mrow><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">s</mi></mrow></msub><mo>+</mo><msub><mrow><mi>R</mi></mrow><mrow><mi>ct</mi></mrow></msub><mo>+</mo><mi>k</mi><msup><mrow><mi>ω</mi></mrow><mrow><mo>−</mo><mn>1</mn><mo>/</mo><mn>2</mn></mrow></msup></mstyle></mrow></math></script></div><div class="label"><span class="labelSpan">(4)</span></div></div>where <i>Z</i><sub>re</sub> is linearly proportional to ω<sup>–1/2</sup> and <i>k</i> is the fitted curve’s slope. It is worth noting that the diffusion coefficient of Na<sup>+</sup> ions in the active material (<i>D</i><sub>Na+</sub>) can be calculated from <a class="ref internalNav" href="#eq5" aria-label="eq 5">eq 5</a>.<div class="MathJaxEquation" id="eq5"><div class="equation"><span class="MathJax_Preview" style="color: inherit;"><span class="MJXp-math MJXp-display" id="MJXp-Span-155"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-156"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-157"><span class="MJXp-mstyle" id="MJXp-Span-158"><span class="MJXp-msub" id="MJXp-Span-159"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-160" style="margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-161">D</span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow MJXp-script" id="MJXp-Span-162" style="vertical-align: -0.4em;"><span class="MJXp-msup" id="MJXp-Span-163"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-164" style="margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="MJXp-mi" id="MJXp-Span-165">Na</span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow MJXp-script" id="MJXp-Span-166" style="vertical-align: 0.5em;"><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-167">+</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-168"><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-169" style="margin-left: 0.333em; margin-right: 0.333em;">=</span><span class="MJXp-mstyle" id="MJXp-Span-170"><span class="MJXp-mfrac" id="MJXp-Span-171" style="vertical-align: 0.25em;"><span class="MJXp-box"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-172"><span class="MJXp-msup" id="MJXp-Span-173"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-174" style="margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-175">R</span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow MJXp-script" id="MJXp-Span-176" style="vertical-align: 0.5em;"><span class="MJXp-mn" id="MJXp-Span-177">2</span></span></span><span class="MJXp-msup" id="MJXp-Span-178"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-179" style="margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-180">T</span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow MJXp-script" id="MJXp-Span-181" style="vertical-align: 0.5em;"><span class="MJXp-mn" id="MJXp-Span-182">2</span></span></span></span></span><span class="MJXp-box" style="margin-top: -0.9em;"><span class="MJXp-denom"><span><span class="MJXp-rule" style="height: 1em; border-top: none; border-bottom: 1px solid; margin: 0.1em 0px;"></span></span><span><span class="MJXp-box"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-183"><span class="MJXp-mn" id="MJXp-Span-184">2</span><span class="MJXp-msup" id="MJXp-Span-185"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-186" style="margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-187">A</span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow MJXp-script" id="MJXp-Span-188" style="vertical-align: 0.5em;"><span class="MJXp-mn" id="MJXp-Span-189">2</span></span></span><span class="MJXp-msup" id="MJXp-Span-190"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-191" style="margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-192">n</span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow MJXp-script" id="MJXp-Span-193" style="vertical-align: 0.5em;"><span class="MJXp-mn" id="MJXp-Span-194">4</span></span></span><span class="MJXp-msup" id="MJXp-Span-195"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-196" style="margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-197">F</span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow MJXp-script" id="MJXp-Span-198" style="vertical-align: 0.5em;"><span class="MJXp-mn" id="MJXp-Span-199">4</span></span></span><span class="MJXp-msup" id="MJXp-Span-200"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-201" style="margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-202">C</span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow MJXp-script" id="MJXp-Span-203" style="vertical-align: 0.5em;"><span class="MJXp-mn" id="MJXp-Span-204">2</span></span></span><span class="MJXp-msup" id="MJXp-Span-205"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-206" style="margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-207">k</span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow MJXp-script" id="MJXp-Span-208" style="vertical-align: 0.5em;"><span class="MJXp-mn" id="MJXp-Span-209">2</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><script type="math/mml" id="MathJax-Element-5"><math display="block" indentalign="left"><mrow><mrow><mstyle indentshift="3em" indentshiftlast="3em"><msub><mrow><mi>D</mi></mrow><mrow><msup><mrow><mi>Na</mi></mrow><mrow><mo>+</mo></mrow></msup></mrow></msub></mstyle></mrow></mrow><mrow><mo linebreak="nobreak">=</mo><mstyle indentshift="3em" indentshiftlast="3em"><mfrac><mrow><msup><mrow><mi>R</mi></mrow><mrow><mn>2</mn></mrow></msup><msup><mrow><mi>T</mi></mrow><mrow><mn>2</mn></mrow></msup></mrow><mrow><mn>2</mn><msup><mrow><mi>A</mi></mrow><mrow><mn>2</mn></mrow></msup><msup><mrow><mi>n</mi></mrow><mrow><mn>4</mn></mrow></msup><msup><mrow><mi>F</mi></mrow><mrow><mn>4</mn></mrow></msup><msup><mrow><mi>C</mi></mrow><mrow><mn>2</mn></mrow></msup><msup><mrow><mi>k</mi></mrow><mrow><mn>2</mn></mrow></msup></mrow></mfrac></mstyle></mrow></math></script></div><div class="label"><span class="labelSpan">(5)</span></div></div>where <i>R</i> represents the gas constant (8.314 J mol<sup>–1</sup> K<sup>–1</sup>), <i>T</i> refers to the temperature (298 K), <i>A</i> indicates the electrode area (cm<sup>2</sup>), <i>n</i> represents electrons involved in the redox process, <i>F</i> refers to the Faraday constant (96,500 C mol<sup>–1</sup>), <i>C</i> stands for sodium concentration (1.0 × 10<sup>–3</sup> mol cm<sup>–3</sup>) and <i>k</i> corresponds to the Warburg factor. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref60" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref60" aria-label="reference 60">(60)</a> According to the results fitted in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 4</a>b, Sb@P-N/C has the smallest slope value of <i>k</i><sub>3</sub> = 0.26, suggesting that the Sb@P-N/C composite has the highest diffusion coefficient for Na<sup>+</sup> ions among the compared samples. What important is that the Na<sup>+</sup> ion diffusion coefficient <i>D</i><sub>Na<i>+</i></sub> in Sb@P-N/C can be calculated from <a class="ref internalNav" href="#eq1" aria-label="eq 1">eq 1</a>, and the obtained value is as 0.15 × 10<sup>–7</sup> cm<sup>2</sup>/s. Furthermore, the GITT curves further evaluate the Na<sup>+</sup> ion diffusion coefficient in the Sb@P-N/C electrode and are shown in Supporting Information <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.3c03340/suppl_file/am3c03340_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S13</a>. The CV scans are compared at scanning rates ranging from 0.1, 0.2, 0.3, and 0.4 mV s<sup>–1</sup> to 0.5 mV s<sup>–1</sup> are shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 4</a>c–e, and as seen, all the CV curves display distinct cathode and anode peaks. Apart from that, the <i>I</i><sub>p</sub> and <i>v</i><sup>1/2</sup> are also fitted and plotted in light of the one-to-one correlation between the peak current and the scanning rate.</div><div class="NLM_p">On the basis of the Randles–Sevcik formula (<a class="ref internalNav" href="#eq6" aria-label="eq 6">eq 6</a>):<div class="MathJaxEquation" id="eq6"><div class="equation"><span class="MathJax_Preview" style="color: inherit;"><span class="MJXp-math MJXp-display" id="MJXp-Span-210"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-211"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-212"><span class="MJXp-mstyle" id="MJXp-Span-213"><span class="MJXp-msub" id="MJXp-Span-214"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-215" style="margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-216">I</span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow MJXp-script" id="MJXp-Span-217" style="vertical-align: -0.4em;"><span class="MJXp-mi" id="MJXp-Span-218">p</span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-219"><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-220" style="margin-left: 0.333em; margin-right: 0.333em;">=</span><span class="MJXp-mstyle" id="MJXp-Span-221"><span class="MJXp-mn" id="MJXp-Span-222">0.4463</span><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-223">n</span><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-224">F</span><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-225">A</span><span class="MJXp-msub" id="MJXp-Span-226"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-227" style="margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-228">C</span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow MJXp-script" id="MJXp-Span-229" style="vertical-align: -0.4em;"><span class="MJXp-mn" id="MJXp-Span-230">0</span></span></span><span class="MJXp-msup" id="MJXp-Span-231"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-232" style="margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-233">v</span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow MJXp-script" id="MJXp-Span-234" style="vertical-align: 0.5em;"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-235"><span class="MJXp-mn" id="MJXp-Span-236">1</span></span><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-237">/</span><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-238"><span class="MJXp-mn" id="MJXp-Span-239">2</span></span></span></span><span class="MJXp-msup" id="MJXp-Span-240"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-241" style="margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-242" style="margin-left: 0em; margin-right: 0em;">(</span><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-243">n</span><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-244">F</span><span class="MJXp-msub" id="MJXp-Span-245"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-246" style="margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-247">D</span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow MJXp-script" id="MJXp-Span-248" style="vertical-align: -0.4em;"><span class="MJXp-mn" id="MJXp-Span-249">0</span></span></span><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-250" style="margin-left: 0.111em; margin-right: 0.111em;">/</span><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-251">R</span><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-252">T</span><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-253" style="margin-left: 0em; margin-right: 0em;">)</span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow MJXp-script" id="MJXp-Span-254" style="vertical-align: 0.5em;"><span class="MJXp-mn" id="MJXp-Span-255">1</span><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-256">/</span><span class="MJXp-mn" id="MJXp-Span-257">2</span></span></span></span></span></span></span><script type="math/mml" id="MathJax-Element-6"><math display="block" indentalign="left"><mrow><mrow><mstyle indentshift="3em" indentshiftlast="3em"><msub><mrow><mi>I</mi></mrow><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">p</mi></mrow></msub></mstyle></mrow></mrow><mrow><mo linebreak="nobreak">=</mo><mstyle indentshift="3em" indentshiftlast="3em"><mn>0.4463</mn><mi>n</mi><mi>F</mi><mi>A</mi><msub><mrow><mi>C</mi></mrow><mrow><mn>0</mn></mrow></msub><msup><mrow><mi>v</mi></mrow><mrow><mrow><mn>1</mn></mrow><mo>/</mo><mrow><mn>2</mn></mrow></mrow></msup><msup><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>n</mi><mi>F</mi><msub><mrow><mi>D</mi></mrow><mrow><mn>0</mn></mrow></msub><mo>/</mo><mi>R</mi><mi>T</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mrow><mn>1</mn><mo>/</mo><mn>2</mn></mrow></msup></mstyle></mrow></math></script></div><div class="label"><span class="labelSpan">(6)</span></div></div>where <i>C</i><sub>0</sub> denotes the materials’ initial composition, <i>v</i> represents the scanning speed, and <i>D</i><sub>0</sub> refers to the diffusion coefficient of Na<sup>+</sup> ion in oxide. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref61 ref63 ref64 ref65" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref61 ref63 ref64 ref65" aria-label="reference 61 and 63 to 65">(61,63−65)</a> <a class="ref internalNav" href="#eq6" aria-label="Equation 6">Equation 6</a> provides a qualitative assessment of the diffusion intensity of Na<sup>+</sup> ions in the synthesized materials.</div><div class="NLM_p">To further explore the practical application of fabricated anodes, a full battery with Na(Ni<sub>1/3</sub>Fe<sub>1/3</sub>Mn<sub>1/3</sub>)O<sub>2</sub> as the cathode and Sb@P-N/C as the anode is prepared in a coin-type battery, and <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 5</a>a shows the schematic diagram of the working process, in which Na<sup>+</sup> ions embed and exit the anode during charge and discharge. <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 5</a>b shows the discharging/charging curves for the cathode Na(Ni<sub>1/3</sub>Fe<sub>1/3</sub>Mn<sub>1/3</sub>)O<sub>2</sub> in the voltage window of 2.0–3.0 V, which exhibit a slope in the voltage plateau at 2.6–2.7 V, and <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 5</a>c shows the cycling performance of the fabricated full cell; as shown, the cell can deliver a high reversible specific capacity of 66.8 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> even after being subjected to 60 cycles at 50 mA g<sup>–1</sup>, indicating the unexpected cyclic stability of the full cell. Noteworthy, the specific capacity rises gradually during the first 10 cycles and levels off in the subsequent cycles due to the gradual exposure and the activation of the active material after the charging and discharging processes. In addition, more microscopic characterization and electrochemical performance measurements of the cathode material are also provided in Supporting Information <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.3c03340/suppl_file/am3c03340_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figures S14 and S15</a>. Moreover, the charging/discharging curves of the 3rd, 5th, and 50th cycles that correspond to the Na(Ni<sub>1/3</sub>Fe<sub>1/3</sub>Mn<sub>1/3</sub>)O<sub>2</sub>||Sb@P-N/C full battery are also plotted in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 5</a>d, and from there, it is observed that the measured curves has good overlap with each other, demonstrating the desired reversibility of cathode and anode materials in the sodiation and de-sodiation process. It is confirmed that the as-prepared Sb@P-N/C composite has remarkable potential as an advanced anode material for practical applications in next-generation high-specific energy SIBs.</div><figure id="fig5" data-index="5" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 5</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.3c03340/asset/images/medium/am3c03340_0006.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.3c03340/asset/images/large/am3c03340_0006.jpeg" id="gr5" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 5. (a) Schematic of the working principle of the Na(Ni<sub>1/3</sub>Fe<sub>1/3</sub>Mn<sub>1/3</sub>)O<sub>2</sub>∥Sb@P-N/C full-cell; (b) charge and discharge properties of the Na(Ni<sub>1/3</sub>Fe<sub>1/3</sub>Mn<sub>1/3</sub>)O<sub>2</sub> cathode; (c) cyclic performance of the full cell; (d) charge and discharge properties of the fabricated full cell Na(Ni<sub>1/3</sub>Fe<sub>1/3</sub>Mn<sub>1/3</sub>)O<sub>2</sub>∥Sb@P-N/C.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.3c03340/asset/images/large/am3c03340_0006.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.3c03340&amp;id=fig5"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure></div><div id="sec4" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i14">4.  Conclusions</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p last">In summary, the hexagonal Sb nanocrystals in the Sb@P-N/C nanofibers are successfully synthesized using a simple but effective electrospinning method. Used as the anode for SIBs, the as-produced Sb@P-N/C nanocomposites that are co-doped with P and N elements exhibit unexpected electrochemical performance with high cycling stability and capacity, rendering capacities of 500.1 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at 50 mA g<sup>–1</sup> exceeding 200 cycles and 295.6 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at 500 mA g<sup>–1</sup> after 400 cycles as well as a high rate capability of up to 5.0 A g<sup>–1</sup> with a specific capacity of 249.9 mAh g<sup>–1</sup>. More importantly, the hexagonal Sb nanocrystals not only alleviate the volume expansion of Sb but also enhance the electrical conductivity of the electrode material and prolong the battery’s lifetime. Particularly, it deserves to be noted that the full cell assembled by the Sb@P-N/C anode and Na(Ni<sub>1/3</sub>Fe<sub>1/3</sub>Mn<sub>1/3</sub>)O<sub>2</sub> cathode deliver a reversible specific capacity of 66.8 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> after 60 cycles at 50 mA g<sup>–1</sup>. The current work explored a new class of Sb-based anodes for investigations on Na<sup>+</sup> ion half- and full-cells, which inspire new ideas on designing and fabricating high-capacity cathodes and anodes for the next generation of SIBs.</div></div><div class="NLM_back"><div class="article_supporting-info" id="notes1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i15">Supporting Information</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><p class="last">The Supporting Information is available free of charge at <a href="/doi/10.1021/acsami.3c03340?goto=supporting-info" class="ext-link">https://pubs.acs.org/doi/10.1021/acsami.3c03340</a>.</p><ul class="NLM_list-list_type-label" id="silist"><li><p class="inline">Additional SEM, TEM, Raman, and TG analysis data; electrochemical performance; summary comparison of literature (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.3c03340/suppl_file/am3c03340_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">PDF</a>)</p></li></ul><p></p><div class="supInfoBoxOnFTP "><div class="sup-info-attachments"><ul><li><a class="suppl-anchor" href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.3c03340/suppl_file/am3c03340_si_001.pdf">am3c03340_si_001.pdf (2.1 MB)</a></li></ul></div></div></div><div class="testing" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.3c03340" data-url="https://widgets.figshare.com/static/figshare.js" id="figshare-widget" style="display: block;"></div><div class="TermsAndConditionsDropzone3" data-pb-dropzone="TermsAndConditionsDropzone3"><div data-widget-def="UX3HTMLWidget" data-widget-id="85b54935-30e9-4058-a6d2-0b40fb754a85" class="mb-4">

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Rapid growth in the market for elec. vehicles is imperative, to meet global targets for reducing greenhouse gas emissions, to improve air quality in urban centers and to meet the needs of consumers, with whom elec. vehicles are increasingly popular.  However, growing nos. of elec. vehicles present a serious waste-management challenge for recyclers at end-of-life.  Nevertheless, spent batteries may also present an opportunity as manufacturers require access to strategic elements and crit. materials for key components in elec.-vehicle manuf.: recycled Li-ion batteries from elec. vehicles could provide a valuable secondary source of materials.  Here the authors outline and evaluate the current range of approaches to elec.-vehicle Li-ion battery recycling and re-use, and highlight areas for future progress.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref3"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref3" class="refNumLink">3</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit3" data-doi="10.1016/j.est.2021.103231"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nathalie, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Oliver, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gebrekidan Gebresilassie, E.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Egbert, F.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A Review of the Publication and Patent Landscape of Anode Materials for Lithium-ion Batteries</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit5R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">5</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Model-based health-aware fast charging to mitigate the risk of lithium plating and prolong the cycle life of lithium-ion batteries in electric vehicles</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wassiliadis, Nikolaos; Kriegler, Johannes; Gamra, Kareem Abo; Lienkamp, Markus</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">561</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">232586</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPSODZ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0378-7753</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The obsd. shift to a fully electrified transport sector with steadily increasing sales of battery elec. vehicles has led to their wider use under demanding operation conditions, e.g., more frequent fast charging due to a higher degree of utilization with an increased share of operation under low ambient temps.  These crit. edge cases have to be precisely controlled by the battery management system to avoid accelerated battery aging and, in the worst case, safety-crit. battery failure events.  In this article, we present a model-based, health-aware fast charging strategy for current control of lithium-ion batteries to prevent the onset of non-linear aging and to prolong the cycle life.  An electrochem. model of reduced order is used to avoid non-linear aging due to lithium plating.  The model is regularly updated alongside the state-of-health of the battery to account for the rise of resistance.  Extensive cycle life results reveal that the charging time can be significantly reduced while the cycle life can be prolonged compared to conventional charging.  As the strategy is based on an electrochem. model of reduced order, inheriting the physics of lithium-ion batteries, the results can be easily transferred to other cell chemistries and/or formats.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref6"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref6" class="refNumLink">6</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit6" data-doi="10.3866/PKU.WHXB202106002"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zeng, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mu, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">NH2-MIL-125 (Ti) Derived Flower-Like Fine TiO<sub>2</sub> Nanoparticles Implanted in N-doped Porous Carbon as an Anode with High Activity and Long Cycle Life for Lithium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Acta Phys.-Chim.                         cas_cit8R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">8</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Binding SnO2 Nanocrystals in Nitrogen-Doped Graphene Sheets as Anode Materials for Lithium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhou, Xiaosi; Wan, Li-Jun; Guo, Yu-Guo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">By using in situ hydrazine monohydrate vapor redn. to form SnO2 nanocrystal/nitrogen-doped reduced graphene oxide (SnO2NC@N-RGO) hybrid material, we have enabled SnO2 nanocrystals to approach the theor. capacity of SnO2 as an anode material for lithium-ion batteries.  The as-obtained hybrid SnO2NC@N-RGO also exhibits excellent properties in terms of cycling performance and rate capability as well as cycle life for lithium-ion batteries, benefiting from the nanosized SnO2 particles, the highly conductive graphene, and the Sn-N bond formed between graphene and SnO2 nanocrystals.                         cas_cit10R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">10</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Room-temperature stationary sodium-ion batteries for large-scale electric energy storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Pan, Huilin; Hu, Yong-Sheng; Chen, Liquan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Room-temp. stationary sodium-ion batteries have attracted great attention particularly in large-scale elec. energy storage applications for renewable energy and smart grid because of the huge abundant sodium resources and low cost.  In this article, a variety of electrode materials including cathodes and anodes as well as electrolytes for room-temp. stationary sodium-ion batteries are briefly reviewed.  We compare the difference in storage behavior between Na and Li in their analogous electrodes and summarize the sodium storage mechanisms in the available electrode materials.  This review also includes some new results from our group and our thoughts on developing new materials.  Some perspectives and directions on designing better materials for practical applications are pointed out based on knowledge from the literature and our experience.  Through this extensive literature review, the search for suitable electrode and electrolyte materials for stationary sodium-ion batteries is still challenging.  However, after intensive research efforts, we believe that low-cost, long-life and room-temp. sodium-ion batteries would be promising for applications in large-scale energy storage system in the near future.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref11"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref11" class="refNumLink">11</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit11" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2022.141602"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ning, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiaojing, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiaojiao, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pengfei, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xuli, D.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Mass Produced Sb/P@C Composite Nanospheres for Advanced Sodium-ions Battery Anodes</span>. <i>Electrochim.                         cas_cit12R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">12</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Challenges and perspectives of covalent organic frameworks for advanced alkali-metal ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xu, Jingyi; Xu, Yifan; Lai, Chenling; Xia, Tingting; Zhang, Beining; Zhou, Xiaosi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Science China: Chemistry</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">64</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">8</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1267-1282</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">SCCCCS</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1869-1870</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Science China Press</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Covalent org. frameworks (COFs) are a class of porous cryst. polymers that have been widely investigated in various fields, including energy storage, photo/electrocatalysis, drug delivery.  The covalent-bond interconnection allows COFs extraordinary chem. and thermal stability, and the porous structure ensures a high ion-diffusion coeff.  These merits compensate for the drawbacks of org. electrodes that are easy to dissolve and have low charge cond., and promote the development of novel electrode materials with excellent performance, environmental friendliness, and low price.  However, the application of COFs also encountered many problems, such as poor electronic cond. due to the large band gap.  Moreover, in some three-dimensional (3D) COFs and stacked two-dimensional (2D) COFs, the huge crystal structure, aligned ultralong channels, and numerous crystal defects usually impede ion transport, and the large mol. wts. of COFs generally decrease the specific capacities.  These issues are urgently needed to be solved.  Here in this review, we summarize the latest progress, core challenges and coping strategies concerning with the use of COFs in alkali-metal ion batteries, discuss the impact of material structure on energy storage, and propose strategies for the construction of high-performance COF-based electrodes.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref13"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref13" class="refNumLink">13</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit13" data-doi="10.1039/D2QI01932A"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jun, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chenrui, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jitao, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yangyang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huaixin, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chencheng, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hongbo, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yushen, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Nickel Cobalt Selenides on Black Phosphorene with Fast Electron Transport for High-energy Density Sodium-ion Half/Full Batteries</span>. <i>Inorg.                         cas_cit17R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">17</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Understanding the mechanisms of mixed-ion cathode materials for aqueous and non-aqueous lithium/sodium-ion batteries - A review</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lakshmi, D.; Palaniyandy, Nithyadharseni; Bohm, Sivasambu; Mamba, Bhekie B.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Current Opinion in Electrochemistry</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  In spite of reliability and high-energy d. of lithium-ion batteries (LIBs), scarcity of Li and safety concerns have prompted the need to develop new-alternate systems.  Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are becoming increasingly popular in this regard.  Their progress is hampered by poor electrochem. performances caused by slow Na-ion diffusion-kinetics.  To address these concerns, new concepts and new battery technol., such as the fabrication of hybrid-ion and mixed-ion batteries, have been proposed.  In this review, we explored the significance of mixed-ion batteries and mixed-ion electrolytes for aq. and non-aq. batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref18"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref18" class="refNumLink">18</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit18" data-doi="10.1039/D0TA12063D"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shreya, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sebastian, C.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">An Overview on Sb-based Intermetallics and Alloys for Sodium-ion Batteries: Trends, Challenges and Future Prospects from Material Synthesis to Battery Performance</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit35R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">35</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">BiSb@Bi2O3/SbOx encapsulated in porous carbon as anode materials for sodium/potassium-ion batteries with a high pseudocapacitive contribution</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Zhiyuan; Duan, Chanqin; Wang, Dan; Dong, Kangze; Luo, Shaohua; Liu, Yanguo; Wang, Qing; Zhang, Yahui; Hao, Aimin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Colloid and Interface Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">580</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">429-438</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JCISA5</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0021-9797</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) and potassium-ion batteries (PIBs) are emerging next-generation energy storage technol., and exploiting applicative electrode materials to accommodate the large-sized Na+ and K+ are urgently needed.  Herein, an innovative composite of BiSb@Bi2O3/SbOx nanoparticles encapsulated in porous carbon (BiSb@Bi2O3/SbOx@C) is fabricated through a template-assisted in-situ pyrogenic decompn. and evaluated as anodes for SIBs and PIBs.  The BiSb@Bi2O3/SbOx@C delivers high specific capacity, superior rate capability (205 mA h g-1 and 111 mA h g-1 at 2 Ah g-1) and good cycling stability (248 mA h g-1 and 214 mA h g-1 after 500 cycles at 1 A g-1) in SIBs and PIBs.  The excellent performance owes to the synergistic effect of Bi and Sb, the multilayer nanostructure design as well as the interconnected porous carbon network, which effectively promotes electron transport and ion diffusion, restricts vol. change and enhances the electrode structure stability simultaneously.  Furthermore, the capacitive behavior contributes much to the storage of sodium and potassium ions, which guarantees a superior rate capability.  This research opens up new opportunities for exploring high-performance anodes for SIBs and PIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref36"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref36" class="refNumLink">36</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit36" data-doi="10.1016/j.ijhydene.2021.02.157"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xianyang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiakang, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zuojun, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hongwei, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huayi, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Electrochemically Converting Sb2S3/CNTs to Sb/CNTs Composite Anodes for Sodium-ion Batteries</span>. <i>Int.                         cas_cit39R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">39</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Three dimensional self-assembly ZnSb nanowire balls with good performance as sodium ions battery anode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liao, S.; Sun, Y.; Wang, Jing; Cui, H.; Wang, Chengxin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">211</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">11-17</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ELCAAV</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0013-4686</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Novel 3D ZnSb nanowire balls composed of ultra-thin nanowires were achieved through simple self-assembly method based on typical thermodn. in chem. vapor deposition (CVD) system.  The elliptic cylinder-shaped nanowires with cross-section size of ∼25nm × ∼ 10 nm display impressive performance in sodium-ion battery (SIB) application as anode material.  Comparing to pure Sb, ZnSb is advantageous in resisting huge vol. change and possess enhanced cond., which would do much better to offer a long-time cycling stability and rate performance.  Such a small size of the low dimensional structures can further improve the electron/ion transfer efficiency.  Through systematic measurements, we found that, at 20 mA/g, the capacity remains 377mAh/g after the 100th cycle with the coulombic efficiency at ∼99%.  Even if the c.d. increased to 750 mA/g, the value was still higher than 225mAh/g.  The half-cell device also provides a rapid response and stable output in the rate tests (20-650 mA/g).  The good performance originates from the unique structural configuration, implying the huge potential value of ZnSb in SIB application.  We hope the results also can expand the Sb based anode material family.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref40"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref40" class="refNumLink">40</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit40" data-doi="10.1002/celc.202001252"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guoju, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shuyi, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lianfeng, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xueyu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liying, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xijia, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xuesong, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wei, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">The Dual Capacity Contribution Mechanism of SnSb-Anchored Nitrogen-Doped 3D Reduced Graphene Oxide Enhances the Performance of Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>ChemElectroChem</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>7</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">4663</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">4671</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Controllable Synthesis of Peapod-like Sb@C and Corn-like C@Sb Nanotubes for Sodium Storage</span>. <i>ACS Nano</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>14</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">5728</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">5737</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acsnano.0c00366</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D14%26publication_year%3D2020%26pages%3D5728-5737%26journal%3DACS%2BNano%26author%3DK.%2BYang%26author%3DJ.%2BTang%26author%3DY.%2BLiu%26author%3DM.%2BKong%26author%3DB.%2BZhou%26author%3DY.%2BShang%26author%3DW.%2BH.%2BZhang%26title%3DControllable%2BSynthesis%2Bof%2BPeapod-like%2BSb%2540C%2Band%2BCorn-like%2BC%2540Sb%2BNanotubes%2Bfor%2BSodium%2BStorage%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facsnano.0c00366&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.3c03340&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facsnano.0c00366&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit45R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">45</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Controllable Synthesis of Peapod-like Sb@C and Corn-like C@Sb Nanotubes for Sodium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yang, Kaixuan; Tang, Jianfeng; Liu, Yan; Kong, Ming; Zhou, Bin; Shang, Yongchen; Zhang, Wen-Hua</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">14</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">5</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">5728-5737</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Antimony (Sb) is regarded as an attractive anode material for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) due to its high theor. capacity of 660 mAh g-1.  Combining Sb with carbonaceous materials has been considered as an effective way to resolve the serious vol. expansion issues.  Sb/C composites mainly consist of two types, i.e., Sb confined inside a carbon matrix and Sb deposited on the surface of a carbon matrix, and both have shown superior sodium storage performance.  However, which structure is more beneficial for achieving high electrochem. performance is still unclear.  In this work, peapod-like Sb@C and corn-like C@Sb nanotubes are synthesized via a nanoconfined galvanic replacement reaction and used as model materials for sodium storage to explore the above issue.  When evaluated as anode materials for SIBs, the peapod-like Sb@C shows a higher rate capability and a significantly better long-term cycling stability compared to those of the corn-like C@Sb.  Electrochem. anal. reveals that the peapod-like Sb@C exhibits faster Na+ and electron transport kinetics and higher proportions of surface capacitive contributions.  These results demonstrate the structural superiority of the nanoconfined structure and provide valuable information for the rational design and construction of Sb-based anode materials for high-performance electrochem. energy storage.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref46"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref46" class="refNumLink">46</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit46" data-doi="10.1039/D0SE01089H"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, W.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Highly Flexible Free-Standing Sb/Sb2O3 @N-doped Carbon Nanofibers Membranes for Sodium Ion Batteries with Excellent Stability</span>. <i>Sustainable Energy Fuels</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>4</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">5732</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">5738</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/D0SE01089H</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D4%26publication_year%3D2020%26pages%3D5732-5738%26journal%3DSustainable%2BEnergy%2BFuels%26author%3DD.%2BLi%26author%3DJ.%2BLi%26author%3DJ.%2BCao%26author%3DX.%2BFu%26author%3DL.%2BZhou%26author%3DW.%2BHan%26title%3DHighly%2BFlexible%2BFree-Standing%2BSb%252FSb2O3%2B%2540N-doped%2BCarbon%2BNanofibers%2BMembranes%2Bfor%2BSodium%2BIon%2BBatteries%2Bwith%2BExcellent%2BStability%26doi%3D10.1039%252FD0SE01089H&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.3c03340&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2FD0SE01089H&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit46R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">46</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Highly flexible free-standing Sb/Sb2O3@N-doped carbon nanofiber membranes for sodium ion batteries with excellent stability</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Dongdong; Li, Junzhi; Cao, Junming; Fu, Xiyao; Zhou, Liang; Han, Wei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Sustainable Energy &amp; Fuels</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">4</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">5732-5738</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">SEFUA7</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2398-4902</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sb and Sb2O3 are attractive anode materials for sodium ion batteries due to their relatively low cost and high theor. capacity.  However, the poor cycling stability caused by serious vol. expansion hinders their development.  In this work, we use electrospinning and carbon thermal redn. to easily synthesize Sb/Sb2O3@N-doped carbon nanofiber membranes.  The flexible Sb/Sb2O3@NCNF membranes are directly used as free-standing electrodes in SIBs showing a high specific capacity and excellent cycling stability (527.3 mA h g-1 after 100 cycles at 0.1 A g-1).  They can still deliver a reversible specific capacity around 400 mA h g-1 after 700 cycles even at 1 A g-1.  The flexible free-standing design, simple synthesis methods and excellent electrochem. properties make the Sb/Sb2O3@NCNF electrodes an ideal anode candidate material for sodium ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref47"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref47" class="refNumLink">47</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit47" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201601973"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yanying, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pengfei, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kaixiang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qing, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhanliang, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jun, C.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Selenium Phosphide (Se4P4) as a New and Promising Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit50R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">50</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Novel hybrid of amorphous Sb/N-doped layered carbon for high-performance sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yang, Jian; Li, Jiabao; Wang, Tianyi; Notten, Peter H. L.; Ma, Hao; Liu, Zhigang; Wang, Chengyin; Wang, Guoxiu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">407</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">127169</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CMEJAJ</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Antimony (Sb) based materials, which have been proved to be promising anodes to fabricate high-performance sodium-ion batteries (SIBs), have attracted considerable interest owing to its large theor. capacity (660 mAh g-1), appropriate inserting potential of sodium (0.5-0.8 V vs Na+/Na), and moderate electrode polarization (∼0.35 V).  Unfortunately, fast capacity decay and serious structure pulverization resulting from large vol. variation upon cycling are often obsd. for Sb-based anodes, and further structure design is needed.  In this work, a novel hybrid of amorphous Sb/N-doped layered carbon (a-Sb/NC) was fabricated through a facile bottom-up method, where ultrafine amorphous Sb nanoparticles are uniformly anchored on layered N-doped carbon (NC).  When applied as anode material for SIBs, this hybrid exhibits a large reversible capacity (479.6 mAh g-1 at 0.1 A g-1 up to 100 cycles), robust rate capability (298.7 mAh g-1 at c.d. of 2 A g-1), and remarkable stability upon long-term cycling (280.5 mAh g-1 at 1.0 A g-1 up to 500 cycles), outperforming most of the reported amorphous anodes for SIBs.  In principle, such impressive sodium storage properties of a-Sb/NC should be mainly ascribed to the amorphous feature of Sb nanoparticles as well as the synergistic effect between amorphous Sb and layered NC, thereby endowing the composite with improved electron/ion dynamics and efficient self-buffering ability.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref51"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref51" class="refNumLink">51</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit51" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2017.03.055"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xuli, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yangyang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guolong, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiaocheng, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yunhui, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Phosphorus Nanoparticles Combined with Cubic Boron Nitride and Graphene as Stable Sodium-ion Battery Anodes</span>. <i>Electrochim.                         cas_cit53R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">53</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Encapsulation of Red Phosphorus in Carbon Nanocages with Ultrahigh Content for High-Capacity and Long Cycle Life Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Weili; Du, Lingyu; Ju, Shunlong; Cheng, Xueyi; Wu, Qiang; Hu, Zheng; Yu, Xuebin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">15</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">3</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">5679-5688</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Red phosphorus (RP) has attracted great attention as a potential candidate for anode materials of high-energy d. sodium-ion batteries (NIBs) due to its high theor. capacity, appropriate working voltage, and natural abundance.  However, the low elec. conductance and huge volumetric variation during the sodiation-desodiation process, causing poor rate performance and cyclability, have limited the practical application of RP in NIBs.  Herein, we report a rational strategy to resolve these issues by encapsulating nanoscaled RP into conductive and networked carbon nanocages (denoted as RP@CNCs) using a combination of a phosphorus-amine based method and evacuation-filling process.  The large interior cavities vol. of CNCs and controllable soln.-based method enable the ultrahigh RP loading amt. (85.3 wt %) in the RP@CNC composite.  Benefiting from the synergic effects of the interior cavities and conductive network, which afford high structure stability and rapid electron transport, the RP@CNC composite presents a high systematic capacity of 1363 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 100 mA g-1 after 150 cycles, favorable high-rate capability, and splendid long-cycling performance with capacity retention over 80% after 1300 cycles at 5000 mA g-1.  This prototypical design promises an efficient soln. to maximize RP loading as well as to boost the electrochem. performance of RP-based anodes.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref54"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref54" class="refNumLink">54</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit54" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.202000060"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiao, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Banis, M. Funct. Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>30</i></span>, <span class="NLM_elocation-id">2000060</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit54R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">54</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Understanding the Critical Role of Binders in Phosphorus/Carbon Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries through Unexpected Mechanism</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xiao, Wei; Sun, Qian; Banis, Mohammad Norouzi; Wang, Biqiong; Li, Weihan; Li, Minsi; Lushington, Andrew; Li, Ruying; Li, Xifei; Sham, Tsun-Kong; Sun, Xueliang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">30</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">32</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2000060</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AFMDC6</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1616-301X</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Polymer binders that combine active materials with conductive agents have played a crit. role in maintaining the structural integrity of phosphorus anodes with a huge vol. change upon sodiation/desodiation.  Herein, the role of binders on the structural/chem. stability of phosphorus/carbon anode is spectroscopically uncovered through unexpected mechanism.  Surprisingly, the selection of different binders is found to det. the oxidn. degree of active phosphorus in various electrodes, which correlate well with their electrochem. properties.  At a high oxidn. degree, the electrode applying a conventional poly(vinylidene difluoride) binder displays the worst electrochem. properties, while the electrode using a sodium alginate binder delivers the best electrochem. performance (a highly reversible capacity of 1064 mAh g-1 with a 90.1% capacity retention at 800 mA g-1 after 200 cycles and an outstanding rate capability of 401 mAh g-1 at 8000 mA g-1) for its negligible oxidn.  This novel discovery of the unique role of binders in phosphorus anodes, not only provides an opportunity to ameliorate their electrochem. properties, but also enables their practical applications in high-energy sodium-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref55"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref55" class="refNumLink">55</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit55" data-doi="10.1016/j.matt.2019.03.010"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jing, W.
