C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, Q.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">N-Doped Carbon Nanonecklaces with Encapsulated Sb as a Sodium-Ion Battery Anode</span>. <i>Matter</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>1</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">720</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">733</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.matt.2019.03.010</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D1%26publication_year%3D2019%26pages%3D720-733%26journal%3DMatter%26author%3DW.%2BT.%2BJing%26author%3DY.%2BZhang%26author%3DY.%2BGu%26author%3DY.%2BF.%2BZhu%26author%3DC.%2BC.%2BYang%26author%3DQ.%2BJiang%26title%3DN-Doped%2BCarbon%2BNanonecklaces%2Bwith%2BEncapsulated%2BSb%2Bas%2Ba%2BSodium-Ion%2BBattery%2BAnode%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.matt.2019.03.010&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.3c03340&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.matt.2019.03.010&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit55R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">55</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">N-Doped Carbon Nanonecklaces with Encapsulated Sb as a Sodium-Ion Battery Anode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Jing, Wen Tao; Zhang, Ying; Gu, Yan; Zhu, Yong Fu; Yang, Chun Cheng; Jiang, Qing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Matter</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">1</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">3</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">720-733</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">MATTCG</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2590-2385</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Inc.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The sodium-ion battery has shown great potential to replace the lithium-ion battery, esp. for large-scale energy-storage systems.  In this work, a hybrid material of ultra-small Sb nanoparticles encapsulated in unique N-doped carbon nanonecklace (Sb/N-CNN) has been synthesized for the first time via electrospinning and in situ substitution.  As an anode material in sodium-ion batteries, the as-fabricated Sb/N-CNN exhibits superior rate property (314 mAh g-1 at 20 A g-1) and cycling stability (401 mAh g-1 after 6,000 cycles at 1 A g-1), outperforming other Sb-based materials.  Such excellent performances originate from the ingenious necklace-like structure of Sb/N-CNN, which supplies efficient electrolyte diffusion paths and more active sites for Na+ insertion/extn., disperses the stress caused by the large vol. change of Sb nanoparticles during the cycling process, and also reduces the electrode resistance.  This study provides a facile strategy for construction of a well-designed structure for advanced energy-storage technologies.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref56"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref56" class="refNumLink">56</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit56" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.9b23501"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fan, X. Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gou, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, D. L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ding, Y. L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">3D Porous Self-Standing Sb Foam Anode with a Conformal Indium Layer for Enhanced Sodium Storage</span>. <i>ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>12</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">20344</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">20353</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acsami.9b23501</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D12%26publication_year%3D2020%26pages%3D20344-20353%26journal%3DACS%2BAppl.%2BMater.%2BInterfaces%26author%3DX.%2BY.%2BFan%26author%3DZ.%2BJiang%26author%3DL.%2BHuang%26author%3DX.%2BWang%26author%3DJ.%2BHan%26author%3DR.%2BSun%26author%3DL.%2BGou%26author%3DD.%2BL.%2BLi%26author%3DY.%2BL.%2BDing%26title%3D3D%2BPorous%2BSelf-Standing%2BSb%2BFoam%2BAnode%2Bwith%2Ba%2BConformal%2BIndium%2BLayer%2Bfor%2BEnhanced%2BSodium%2BStorage%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facsami.9b23501&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.3c03340&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facsami.9b23501&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit56R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">56</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">3D Porous Self-Standing Sb Foam Anode with a Conformal Indium Layer for Enhanced Sodium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Fan, Xiao-Yong; Jiang, Zhen; Huang, Long; Wang, Xinxin; Han, Jiaxing; Sun, Ruibo; Gou, Lei; Li, Dong-Lin; Ding, Yuan-Li</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">12</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">18</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">20344-20353</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1944-8244</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Antimony (Sb) has been considered as a promising anode for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) because of its high theor. capacity and moderate working potential but suffers from the dramatic vol. variations (~ 250%), an unstable electrode/electrolyte interphase, active material exfoliation, and a continuously increased interphase impedance upon sodiation and desodiation processes.  To address these issues, we report a unique three-dimensional (3D) porous self-standing foam electrode built from core-shelled Sb@In2O3 nanostructures via a continuous electrodepositing strategy coupled with surface chem. passivation.  Such a hierarchical structure possesses a robust framework with rich voids and a dense protection layer (In2O3), which allow Sb nanoparticles to well accommodate their mech. strain for efficiently avoiding electrode cracks and pulverization with a stable electrode/electrolyte interphase upon sodiation/desodiation processes.  When evaluated as an anode for SIBs, the prepd. nanoarchitectures exhibit a high first reversible capacity (641.3 mA h g-1) and good cyclability (456.5 mA h g-1 after 300 cycles at 300 mA g-1), along with superior high rate capacity (348.9 mA h g-1 even at 20 A g-1) with a first Coulomb efficiency as high as 85.3%.  This work could offer an efficient approach to improve alloying-based anode materials for promoting their practical applications.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref57"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref57" class="refNumLink">57</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit57" data-doi="10.1038/s41467-022-35617-3"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qiulong, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiaoqing, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Danielle, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ryan, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kun, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Junbin, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dongliang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dong-Liang, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bruce, D.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Surface-redox Sodium-ion Storage in Anatase Titanium Oxide</span>. <i>Nat.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sulfidic sodium ion conductors are currently investigated for the possible use in all-solid-state sodium ion batteries.  The design of high-performing electrolytes in terms of temp.-dependent ionic transport is based upon the fundamental understanding of structure-transport relationships within the given structural phase boundaries inherent to the investigated materials class.  In this work, the Na+ superionic structural family of Na11Sn2PS12 is explored by using the systematic antimony substitution with phosphorus in Na11+xSn2+x(Sb1-yPy)1-xS12.  A combination of Rietveld refinements against X-ray synchrotron diffraction data with electrochem. impedance spectroscopy is used to monitor the changes in the anionic framework, the Na+ substructure, and the ionic transport.  A new simplified descriptor for the av. Na+ diffusion pathways, the av. Na+ polyhedral vol., is introduced, which is used to correlate the contraction of the overall lattice and the found activation barriers in the system.  This study exemplifies how substitution affects diffusion pathways in ionic conductors and widens the knowledge about the related structural motifs and their influence on the ionic transport in this novel class of ionic conductors.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref63"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref63" class="refNumLink">63</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit63" data-doi="10.1016/j.scriptamat.2022.114860"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wen, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bai, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Z.-D.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Bismuth Oxychloride Clusters Prepared by Ball-milling Technique and Their Multifunctional Application in Potassium Ion Storage and Photodegradation</span>. <i>Scripta Mater</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2022</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>219</i></span>, <span class="NLM_elocation-id">114860</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.scriptamat.2022.114860</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D219%26publication_year%3D2022%26journal%3DScripta%2BMater%26author%3DJ.%2BWu%26author%3DL.%2BZhang%26author%3DZ.%2BYan%26author%3DJ.%2BWen%26author%3DJ.%2BChang%26author%3DY.%2BZhang%26author%3DL.%2BBai%26author%3DZ.%2BLi%26author%3DZ.-D.%2BHuang%26title%3DBismuth%2BOxychloride%2BClusters%2BPrepared%2Bby%2BBall-milling%2BTechnique%2Band%2BTheir%2BMultifunctional%2BApplication%2Bin%2BPotassium%2BIon%2BStorage%2Band%2BPhotodegradation%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.scriptamat.2022.114860&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.3c03340&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.scriptamat.2022.114860&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit63R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">63</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Bismuth oxychloride clusters prepared by ball-milling technique and their multifunctional application in potassium ion storage and photodegradation</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wu, Jingjing; Zhang, Lida; Yan, Zhongyuan; Wen, Jinquan; Chang, Jing; Zhang, Yifan; Bai, Ling; Li, Ziquan; Huang, Zhen-Dong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Scripta Materialia</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">219</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">114860</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">SCMAF7</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1359-6462</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">BiOCl is a promising anode material for potassium ion batteries and also one of the potential candidate catalysts for photocatalytic degrdn. of org. pollutants.  Here, a wet ball-milling assisted hydrolysis method is proposed to produce the desired BiOCl.  During the hydrolysis process under the ball-milling condition, the obtained BiOCl nanosheets self-assemble into flower-like micro-clusters with a uniform distribution of Bi3+, O2-, Cl- and a low BET sp. surface area.  Esp., the obtained BOCl clusters demonstrate a superior potassium ion storage performance over most of the reported BiOCl and comparable photocatalytic degrdn. properties of Rhodamine B.  The charge capacity of BiOCl electrodes retained 373 mAhg-1 after 300 cycles at 100 mAg-1 and 232 mAhg-1 after 1000 cycles at 500 mAg-1, resp. ∼96.7% RhB in the aq. soln. can be degraded after 60 min of light irradn. under a 300 W xenon lamp.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref64"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref64" class="refNumLink">64</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit64" data-doi="10.1002/adma.202105404"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yangyang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yongcheng, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Anmin, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Haoyu, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhiwei, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xueping, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shu-Chih, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jin-Ming, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ting-Shan, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sijie, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiantao, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wei, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yunhui, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Enabling Anionic Redox Stability of P2-Na5/6Li1/4Mn3/4O2 by Mg Substitution</span>. <i>Adv.                 10.1002/adma.202105404</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D34%26publication_year%3D2022%26pages%3D2105404%26journal%3DAdv.%2BMater.%26author%3DH.%2BYangyang%26author%3DZ.%2BYongcheng%26author%3DN.%2BAnmin%26author%3DF.%2BHaoyu%26author%3DH.%2BZhiwei%26author%3DS.%2BXueping%26author%3DH.%2BShu-Chih%26author%3DC.%2BJin-Ming%26author%3DC.%2BTing-Shan%26author%3DY.%2BSijie%26author%3DS.%2BGuang%26author%3DJ.%2BGang%26author%3DH.%2BJiantao%26author%3DL.%2BWei%26author%3DH.%2BYunhui%26title%3DEnabling%2BAnionic%2BRedox%2BStability%2Bof%2BP2-Na5%252F6Li1%252F4Mn3%252F4O2%2Bby%2BMg%2BSubstitution%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fadma.202105404&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.3c03340&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fadma.202105404&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord empty" id="

Power Sources</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2023</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>561</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">232586</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.jpowsour.2022.232586</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit5R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">5</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Model-based health-aware fast charging to mitigate the risk of lithium plating and prolong the cycle life of lithium-ion batteries in electric vehicles</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wassiliadis, Nikolaos; Kriegler, Johannes; Gamra, Kareem Abo; Lienkamp, Markus</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">561</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">232586</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPSODZ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0378-7753</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The obsd. shift to a fully electrified transport sector with steadily increasing sales of battery elec. vehicles has led to their wider use under demanding operation conditions, e.g., more frequent fast charging due to a higher degree of utilization with an increased share of operation under low ambient temps.  These crit. edge cases have to be precisely controlled by the battery management system to avoid accelerated battery aging and, in the worst case, safety-crit. battery failure events.  In this article, we present a model-based, health-aware fast charging strategy for current control of lithium-ion batteries to prevent the onset of non-linear aging and to prolong the cycle life.  An electrochem. model of reduced order is used to avoid non-linear aging due to lithium plating.  The model is regularly updated alongside the state-of-health of the battery to account for the rise of resistance.  Extensive cycle life results reveal that the charging time can be significantly reduced while the cycle life can be prolonged compared to conventional charging.  As the strategy is based on an electrochem. model of reduced order, inheriting the physics of lithium-ion batteries, the results can be easily transferred to other cell chemistries and/or formats.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref6"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref6" class="rightTabRefNumLink">6</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit6" data-doi="10.3866/PKU.WHXB202106002"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zeng, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mu, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">NH2-MIL-125 (Ti) Derived Flower-Like Fine TiO<sub>2</sub> Nanoparticles Implanted in N-doped Porous Carbon as an Anode with High Activity and Long Cycle Life for Lithium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Acta Phys.-Chim. Sin.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2021</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>38</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">2106002</span></span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord empty" id="

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Room-temp. stationary sodium-ion batteries have attracted great attention particularly in large-scale elec. energy storage applications for renewable energy and smart grid because of the huge abundant sodium resources and low cost.  In this article, a variety of electrode materials including cathodes and anodes as well as electrolytes for room-temp. stationary sodium-ion batteries are briefly reviewed.  We compare the difference in storage behavior between Na and Li in their analogous electrodes and summarize the sodium storage mechanisms in the available electrode materials.  This review also includes some new results from our group and our thoughts on developing new materials.  Some perspectives and directions on designing better materials for practical applications are pointed out based on knowledge from the literature and our experience.  Through this extensive literature review, the search for suitable electrode and electrolyte materials for stationary sodium-ion batteries is still challenging.  However, after intensive research efforts, we believe that low-cost, long-life and room-temp. sodium-ion batteries would be promising for applications in large-scale energy storage system in the near future.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref11"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref11" class="rightTabRefNumLink">11</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit11" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2022.141602"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ning, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiaojing, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiaojiao, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pengfei, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xuli, D.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Mass Produced Sb/P@C Composite Nanospheres for Advanced Sodium-ions Battery Anodes</span>. <i>Electrochim.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Covalent org. frameworks (COFs) are a class of porous cryst. polymers that have been widely investigated in various fields, including energy storage, photo/electrocatalysis, drug delivery.  The covalent-bond interconnection allows COFs extraordinary chem. and thermal stability, and the porous structure ensures a high ion-diffusion coeff.  These merits compensate for the drawbacks of org. electrodes that are easy to dissolve and have low charge cond., and promote the development of novel electrode materials with excellent performance, environmental friendliness, and low price.  However, the application of COFs also encountered many problems, such as poor electronic cond. due to the large band gap.  Moreover, in some three-dimensional (3D) COFs and stacked two-dimensional (2D) COFs, the huge crystal structure, aligned ultralong channels, and numerous crystal defects usually impede ion transport, and the large mol. wts. of COFs generally decrease the specific capacities.  These issues are urgently needed to be solved.  Here in this review, we summarize the latest progress, core challenges and coping strategies concerning with the use of COFs in alkali-metal ion batteries, discuss the impact of material structure on energy storage, and propose strategies for the construction of high-performance COF-based electrodes.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref13"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref13" class="rightTabRefNumLink">13</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit13" data-doi="10.1039/D2QI01932A"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jun, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chenrui, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jitao, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yangyang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huaixin, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chencheng, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hongbo, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yushen, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Nickel Cobalt Selenides on Black Phosphorene with Fast Electron Transport for High-energy Density Sodium-ion Half/Full Batteries</span>. <i>Inorg.                         rightTab-cas_cit35R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">35</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">BiSb@Bi2O3/SbOx encapsulated in porous carbon as anode materials for sodium/potassium-ion batteries with a high pseudocapacitive contribution</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Zhiyuan; Duan, Chanqin; Wang, Dan; Dong, Kangze; Luo, Shaohua; Liu, Yanguo; Wang, Qing; Zhang, Yahui; Hao, Aimin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Colloid and Interface Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">580</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">429-438</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JCISA5</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0021-9797</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) and potassium-ion batteries (PIBs) are emerging next-generation energy storage technol., and exploiting applicative electrode materials to accommodate the large-sized Na+ and K+ are urgently needed.  Herein, an innovative composite of BiSb@Bi2O3/SbOx nanoparticles encapsulated in porous carbon (BiSb@Bi2O3/SbOx@C) is fabricated through a template-assisted in-situ pyrogenic decompn. and evaluated as anodes for SIBs and PIBs.  The BiSb@Bi2O3/SbOx@C delivers high specific capacity, superior rate capability (205 mA h g-1 and 111 mA h g-1 at 2 Ah g-1) and good cycling stability (248 mA h g-1 and 214 mA h g-1 after 500 cycles at 1 A g-1) in SIBs and PIBs.  The excellent performance owes to the synergistic effect of Bi and Sb, the multilayer nanostructure design as well as the interconnected porous carbon network, which effectively promotes electron transport and ion diffusion, restricts vol. change and enhances the electrode structure stability simultaneously.  Furthermore, the capacitive behavior contributes much to the storage of sodium and potassium ions, which guarantees a superior rate capability.  This research opens up new opportunities for exploring high-performance anodes for SIBs and PIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref36"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref36" class="rightTabRefNumLink">36</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit36" data-doi="10.1016/j.ijhydene.2021.02.157"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xianyang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiakang, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zuojun, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hongwei, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huayi, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Electrochemically Converting Sb2S3/CNTs to Sb/CNTs Composite Anodes for Sodium-ion Batteries</span>. <i>Int.                         rightTab-cas_cit39R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">39</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Three dimensional self-assembly ZnSb nanowire balls with good performance as sodium ions battery anode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liao, S.; Sun, Y.; Wang, Jing; Cui, H.; Wang, Chengxin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Novel 3D ZnSb nanowire balls composed of ultra-thin nanowires were achieved through simple self-assembly method based on typical thermodn. in chem. vapor deposition (CVD) system.  The elliptic cylinder-shaped nanowires with cross-section size of ∼25nm × ∼ 10 nm display impressive performance in sodium-ion battery (SIB) application as anode material.  Comparing to pure Sb, ZnSb is advantageous in resisting huge vol. change and possess enhanced cond., which would do much better to offer a long-time cycling stability and rate performance.  Such a small size of the low dimensional structures can further improve the electron/ion transfer efficiency.  Through systematic measurements, we found that, at 20 mA/g, the capacity remains 377mAh/g after the 100th cycle with the coulombic efficiency at ∼99%.  Even if the c.d. increased to 750 mA/g, the value was still higher than 225mAh/g.  The half-cell device also provides a rapid response and stable output in the rate tests (20-650 mA/g).  The good performance originates from the unique structural configuration, implying the huge potential value of ZnSb in SIB application.  We hope the results also can expand the Sb based anode material family.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref40"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref40" class="rightTabRefNumLink">40</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit40" data-doi="10.1002/celc.202001252"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guoju, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shuyi, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lianfeng, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xueyu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liying, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xijia, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xuesong, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wei, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">The Dual Capacity Contribution Mechanism of SnSb-Anchored Nitrogen-Doped 3D Reduced Graphene Oxide Enhances the Performance of Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>ChemElectroChem</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>7</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">4663</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">4671</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        rightTab-cas_cit45R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">45</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Controllable Synthesis of Peapod-like Sb@C and Corn-like C@Sb Nanotubes for Sodium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yang, Kaixuan; Tang, Jianfeng; Liu, Yan; Kong, Ming; Zhou, Bin; Shang, Yongchen; Zhang, Wen-Hua</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Antimony (Sb) is regarded as an attractive anode material for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) due to its high theor. capacity of 660 mAh g-1.  Combining Sb with carbonaceous materials has been considered as an effective way to resolve the serious vol. expansion issues.  Sb/C composites mainly consist of two types, i.e., Sb confined inside a carbon matrix and Sb deposited on the surface of a carbon matrix, and both have shown superior sodium storage performance.  However, which structure is more beneficial for achieving high electrochem. performance is still unclear.  In this work, peapod-like Sb@C and corn-like C@Sb nanotubes are synthesized via a nanoconfined galvanic replacement reaction and used as model materials for sodium storage to explore the above issue.  When evaluated as anode materials for SIBs, the peapod-like Sb@C shows a higher rate capability and a significantly better long-term cycling stability compared to those of the corn-like C@Sb.  Electrochem. anal. reveals that the peapod-like Sb@C exhibits faster Na+ and electron transport kinetics and higher proportions of surface capacitive contributions.  These results demonstrate the structural superiority of the nanoconfined structure and provide valuable information for the rational design and construction of Sb-based anode materials for high-performance electrochem. energy storage.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref46"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref46" class="rightTabRefNumLink">46</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit46" data-doi="10.1039/D0SE01089H"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, W.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Highly Flexible Free-Standing Sb/Sb2O3 @N-doped Carbon Nanofibers Membranes for Sodium Ion Batteries with Excellent Stability</span>. <i>Sustainable Energy Fuels</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>4</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">5732</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">5738</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/D0SE01089H</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit46R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">46</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Highly flexible free-standing Sb/Sb2O3@N-doped carbon nanofiber membranes for sodium ion batteries with excellent stability</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Dongdong; Li, Junzhi; Cao, Junming; Fu, Xiyao; Zhou, Liang; Han, Wei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Sustainable Energy &amp; Fuels</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sb and Sb2O3 are attractive anode materials for sodium ion batteries due to their relatively low cost and high theor. capacity.  However, the poor cycling stability caused by serious vol. expansion hinders their development.  In this work, we use electrospinning and carbon thermal redn. to easily synthesize Sb/Sb2O3@N-doped carbon nanofiber membranes.  The flexible Sb/Sb2O3@NCNF membranes are directly used as free-standing electrodes in SIBs showing a high specific capacity and excellent cycling stability (527.3 mA h g-1 after 100 cycles at 0.1 A g-1).  They can still deliver a reversible specific capacity around 400 mA h g-1 after 700 cycles even at 1 A g-1.  The flexible free-standing design, simple synthesis methods and excellent electrochem. properties make the Sb/Sb2O3@NCNF electrodes an ideal anode candidate material for sodium ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref47"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref47" class="rightTabRefNumLink">47</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit47" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201601973"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yanying, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pengfei, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kaixiang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qing, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhanliang, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jun, C.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Selenium Phosphide (Se4P4) as a New and Promising Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Antimony (Sb) based materials, which have been proved to be promising anodes to fabricate high-performance sodium-ion batteries (SIBs), have attracted considerable interest owing to its large theor. capacity (660 mAh g-1), appropriate inserting potential of sodium (0.5-0.8 V vs Na+/Na), and moderate electrode polarization (∼0.35 V).  Unfortunately, fast capacity decay and serious structure pulverization resulting from large vol. variation upon cycling are often obsd. for Sb-based anodes, and further structure design is needed.  In this work, a novel hybrid of amorphous Sb/N-doped layered carbon (a-Sb/NC) was fabricated through a facile bottom-up method, where ultrafine amorphous Sb nanoparticles are uniformly anchored on layered N-doped carbon (NC).  When applied as anode material for SIBs, this hybrid exhibits a large reversible capacity (479.6 mAh g-1 at 0.1 A g-1 up to 100 cycles), robust rate capability (298.7 mAh g-1 at c.d. of 2 A g-1), and remarkable stability upon long-term cycling (280.5 mAh g-1 at 1.0 A g-1 up to 500 cycles), outperforming most of the reported amorphous anodes for SIBs.  In principle, such impressive sodium storage properties of a-Sb/NC should be mainly ascribed to the amorphous feature of Sb nanoparticles as well as the synergistic effect between amorphous Sb and layered NC, thereby endowing the composite with improved electron/ion dynamics and efficient self-buffering ability.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref51"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref51" class="rightTabRefNumLink">51</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit51" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2017.03.055"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xuli, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yangyang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guolong, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiaocheng, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yunhui, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Phosphorus Nanoparticles Combined with Cubic Boron Nitride and Graphene as Stable Sodium-ion Battery Anodes</span>. <i>Electrochim.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Red phosphorus (RP) has attracted great attention as a potential candidate for anode materials of high-energy d. sodium-ion batteries (NIBs) due to its high theor. capacity, appropriate working voltage, and natural abundance.  However, the low elec. conductance and huge volumetric variation during the sodiation-desodiation process, causing poor rate performance and cyclability, have limited the practical application of RP in NIBs.  Herein, we report a rational strategy to resolve these issues by encapsulating nanoscaled RP into conductive and networked carbon nanocages (denoted as RP@CNCs) using a combination of a phosphorus-amine based method and evacuation-filling process.  The large interior cavities vol. of CNCs and controllable soln.-based method enable the ultrahigh RP loading amt. (85.3 wt %) in the RP@CNC composite.  Benefiting from the synergic effects of the interior cavities and conductive network, which afford high structure stability and rapid electron transport, the RP@CNC composite presents a high systematic capacity of 1363 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 100 mA g-1 after 150 cycles, favorable high-rate capability, and splendid long-cycling performance with capacity retention over 80% after 1300 cycles at 5000 mA g-1.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Polymer binders that combine active materials with conductive agents have played a crit. role in maintaining the structural integrity of phosphorus anodes with a huge vol. change upon sodiation/desodiation.  Herein, the role of binders on the structural/chem. stability of phosphorus/carbon anode is spectroscopically uncovered through unexpected mechanism.  Surprisingly, the selection of different binders is found to det. the oxidn. degree of active phosphorus in various electrodes, which correlate well with their electrochem. properties.  At a high oxidn. degree, the electrode applying a conventional poly(vinylidene difluoride) binder displays the worst electrochem. properties, while the electrode using a sodium alginate binder delivers the best electrochem. performance (a highly reversible capacity of 1064 mAh g-1 with a 90.1% capacity retention at 800 mA g-1 after 200 cycles and an outstanding rate capability of 401 mAh g-1 at 8000 mA g-1) for its negligible oxidn.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The sodium-ion battery has shown great potential to replace the lithium-ion battery, esp. for large-scale energy-storage systems. As an anode material in sodium-ion batteries, the as-fabricated Sb/N-CNN exhibits superior rate property (314 mAh g-1 at 20 A g-1) and cycling stability (401 mAh g-1 after 6,000 cycles at 1 A g-1), outperforming other Sb-based materials.                         rightTab-cas_cit56R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">56</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">3D Porous Self-Standing Sb Foam Anode with a Conformal Indium Layer for Enhanced Sodium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Fan, Xiao-Yong; Jiang, Zhen; Huang, Long; Wang, Xinxin; Han, Jiaxing; Sun, Ruibo; Gou, Lei; Li, Dong-Lin; Ding, Yuan-Li</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Antimony (Sb) has been considered as a promising anode for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) because of its high theor. capacity and moderate working potential but suffers from the dramatic vol. variations (~ 250%), an unstable electrode/electrolyte interphase, active material exfoliation, and a continuously increased interphase impedance upon sodiation and desodiation processes.  To address these issues, we report a unique three-dimensional (3D) porous self-standing foam electrode built from core-shelled Sb@In2O3 nanostructures via a continuous electrodepositing strategy coupled with surface chem. passivation.  Such a hierarchical structure possesses a robust framework with rich voids and a dense protection layer (In2O3), which allow Sb nanoparticles to well accommodate their mech. strain for efficiently avoiding electrode cracks and pulverization with a stable electrode/electrolyte interphase upon sodiation/desodiation processes.  When evaluated as an anode for SIBs, the prepd. nanoarchitectures exhibit a high first reversible capacity (641.3 mA h g-1) and good cyclability (456.5 mA h g-1 after 300 cycles at 300 mA g-1), along with superior high rate capacity (348.9 mA h g-1 even at 20 A g-1) with a first Coulomb efficiency as high as 85.3%.  This work could offer an efficient approach to improve alloying-based anode materials for promoting their practical applications.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref57"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref57" class="rightTabRefNumLink">57</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit57" data-doi="10.1038/s41467-022-35617-3"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qiulong, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiaoqing, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Danielle, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ryan, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kun, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Junbin, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dongliang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dong-Liang, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bruce, D.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Surface-redox Sodium-ion Storage in Anatase Titanium Oxide</span>. <i>Nat.                 10.1021/acs.chemmater.1c01680</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord empty" id="

                10.1016/j.jpowsour.2012.10.077</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord empty" id="
                            rightTab-cas_R
                        "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref62"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref62" class="rightTabRefNumLink">62</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit62" data-doi="10.1021/acs.chemmater.0c01964"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kraft, M. A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gronych, L. M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Famprikis, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ohno, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zeier, W. G.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Structure and Sodium Ion Transport in NaSn(SbP)S</span>. <i>Chem. Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>32</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">6566</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">6576</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acs.chemmater.0c01964</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit62R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">62</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Structure and Sodium Ion Transport in Na11+xSn2+x(Sb1-yPy)1-xS12</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kraft, Marvin A.; Gronych, Lara M.; Famprikis, Theodosios; Ohno, Saneyuki; Zeier, Wolfgang G.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry of Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">32</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">15</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">6566-6576</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CMATEX</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0897-4756</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sulfidic sodium ion conductors are currently investigated for the possible use in all-solid-state sodium ion batteries.  The design of high-performing electrolytes in terms of temp.-dependent ionic transport is based upon the fundamental understanding of structure-transport relationships within the given structural phase boundaries inherent to the investigated materials class.  In this work, the Na+ superionic structural family of Na11Sn2PS12 is explored by using the systematic antimony substitution with phosphorus in Na11+xSn2+x(Sb1-yPy)1-xS12.  A combination of Rietveld refinements against X-ray synchrotron diffraction data with electrochem. impedance spectroscopy is used to monitor the changes in the anionic framework, the Na+ substructure, and the ionic transport.  A new simplified descriptor for the av. Na+ diffusion pathways, the av. Na+ polyhedral vol., is introduced, which is used to correlate the contraction of the overall lattice and the found activation barriers in the system.  This study exemplifies how substitution affects diffusion pathways in ionic conductors and widens the knowledge about the related structural motifs and their influence on the ionic transport in this novel class of ionic conductors.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref63"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref63" class="rightTabRefNumLink">63</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit63" data-doi="10.1016/j.scriptamat.2022.114860"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wen, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bai, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Z.-D.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Bismuth Oxychloride Clusters Prepared by Ball-milling Technique and Their Multifunctional Application in Potassium Ion Storage and Photodegradation</span>. <i>Scripta Mater</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2022</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>219</i></span>, <span class="NLM_elocation-id">114860</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.scriptamat.2022.114860</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit63R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">63</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Bismuth oxychloride clusters prepared by ball-milling technique and their multifunctional application in potassium ion storage and photodegradation</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wu, Jingjing; Zhang, Lida; Yan, Zhongyuan; Wen, Jinquan; Chang, Jing; Zhang, Yifan; Bai, Ling; Li, Ziquan; Huang, Zhen-Dong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Scripta Materialia</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">219</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">114860</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">SCMAF7</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1359-6462</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">BiOCl is a promising anode material for potassium ion batteries and also one of the potential candidate catalysts for photocatalytic degrdn. of org. pollutants.  Here, a wet ball-milling assisted hydrolysis method is proposed to produce the desired BiOCl.  During the hydrolysis process under the ball-milling condition, the obtained BiOCl nanosheets self-assemble into flower-like micro-clusters with a uniform distribution of Bi3+, O2-, Cl- and a low BET sp. surface area.  Esp., the obtained BOCl clusters demonstrate a superior potassium ion storage performance over most of the reported BiOCl and comparable photocatalytic degrdn. properties of Rhodamine B.  The charge capacity of BiOCl electrodes retained 373 mAhg-1 after 300 cycles at 100 mAg-1 and 232 mAhg-1 after 1000 cycles at 500 mAg-1, resp. ∼96.7% RhB in the aq. soln. can be degraded after 60 min of light irradn. under a 300 W xenon lamp.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref64"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref64" class="rightTabRefNumLink">64</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit64" data-doi="10.1002/adma.202105404"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yangyang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yongcheng, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Anmin, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Haoyu, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhiwei, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xueping, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shu-Chih, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jin-Ming, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ting-Shan, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sijie, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiantao, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wei, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yunhui, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Enabling Anionic Redox Stability of P2-Na5/6Li1/4Mn3/4O2 by Mg Substitution</span>. <i>Adv.         <script nonce="931882c73c6854b8-SJC">
(function(){
	
	/*Event Tracking for RIS menu dropdown - Article pages*/

	$('.cit-download-dropdown_button').on('click',function(e)
	{	
		e.preventDefault();
	    gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':'Main'});

	});


	$('.cit-download-dropdown_content ul li').on('click',function(e)
	{	
	//	e.preventDefault();
	    var idx = $(this).index();
	    
	    var label = '';
	    if (idx === 0 ) {
	    	label = 'Citation';
	    } else if (idx === 1 ) {
	    	label = 'Abstract';
	    } else if (idx === 2 ) {
	    	label = 'Reference';
	    } else if (idx === 3 ) {
	    	label = 'More Options';
	    }
	   
	   gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':label});
	});

	$('.header_contnav-next a').on('click', function(e){
        e.preventDefault();
        gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Right Arrow'});
	}); 

 	$('.header_contnav-pre a').on('click', function(e){
	    e.preventDefault();
	     gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Left Arrow'});
	}); 

	$('.share_button').on('click', function(e){
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Share'});
	});

	$("#pane-m1con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Figures'});
	});

	$("#pane-m2con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
	    gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'References'});
	});

	$("#pane-m3con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Supporting Info'});
	});

	$('.tab__close').on('click', function(){
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Close'});
	}); 



})();

</script>

<script nonce="931882c73c6854b8-SJC">
document.addEventListener('DOMContentLoaded', function () {
    const modalContainer = document.querySelector('.my-main-container');

    // Function to show the modal
    function showModal() {
        modalContainer.style.display = 'flex';
        document.querySelector('.overlay').style.display = 'block';
    }

    // Function to hide the modal when the close button is clicked
    function hideModal() {
        modalContainer.style.display = 'none';
        document.querySelector('.overlay').style.display = 'none';
    }

    // Hide the modal initially
    hideModal();

    // Function to handle clicks outside the modal
    function handleClickOutside(event) {
        // const modalContainer = document.querySelector(".my-main-container");
        // Check if the click target is not a child of the modal container
        if (!modalContainer.contains(event.target)) {
            hideModal();
        }
    }

    // Add a click event listener to the close button
    document
        .querySelector('.close-button')
        .addEventListener('click', hideModal);

    // Add a click event listener to the document to handle clicks outside the modal
    document.addEventListener('click', handleClickOutside);

    const screenHeight = window.innerHeight;
    function updateModalPosition() {
        const scrollY = window.scrollY;
        // console.log("scrollY= " + scrollY);
        // modalContainer.style.top = `${50 + scrollY}px`;
        modalContainer.style.top = `${scrollY + screenHeight / 2}px`;
        // console.log("new top= " + modalContainer.style.top);
    }

    // Update the modal position when the user scrolls
    window.addEventListener('scroll', updateModalPosition);

    // Initialize the modal position
    updateModalPosition();

    //---Cookie---
    // Function to set the cookie with a given name, value, and expiration time in days
    function setCookie(name, value, days) {
        var expires = '';
        if (days) {
            var date = new Date();
            date.setTime(date.getTime() + days * 24 * 60 * 60 * 1000);
            expires = '; expires=' + date.toUTCString();
            console.log(expires + 'this is expires dateUTC');
        }
        document.cookie = name + '=' + (value || '') + expires + '; path=/';
        // console.log("document.cookie is: " + document.cookie);
    }

    if (!document.cookie.includes('modalAd')) {
        // Show Modal
        showModal();

        // Set the cookie with the name "modalAd", value "true", and expiration of 3 day
        setCookie('modalAd', 'true', 3);
    } else {
        hideModal();
    }
});

</script>
<link rel="stylesheet" type="text/css" href="/pb-assets/smartgroup_ads/Modal-LeadGen-1691422642793.css">
            
        </div>

<script nonce="931882c73c6854b8-SJC">
    document.addEventListener("DOMContentLoaded", function(){
    // Function to get a Human readable formatted date
    function getFormattedDateForMaintenance() {
        let today = new Date();
        let dd = String(today.getDate()).padStart(2, '0');
        //January is 0
        let mm = String(today.getMonth() + 1).padStart(2, '0'); 
        let yyyy = today.getFullYear();
        
        let daysOfWeek = ['Sunday', 'Monday', 'Tuesday', 'Wednesday', 'Thursday', 'Friday', 'Saturday'];
        let monthsOfYear = ['January', 'February', 'March', 'April', 'May', 'June', 'July', 'August', 'September', 'October', 'November', 'December'];

        let dayOfWeek = daysOfWeek[today.getDay()];
        let monthOfYear = monthsOfYear[today.getMonth()];

        return dayOfWeek + ', ' + monthOfYear + ' ' + dd + ', ' + yyyy;
    }
    
    // Insert the date into the .system-message-date element
    document.querySelector('.system-message-date').innerText = getFormattedDateForMaintenance();
});
</script>

      var emailValid = "",
        time = 3000,
        btnStatus = true,
        errorStatus = false,
        errormessage =
          "<p class='gdpr_err'><b>Please Enter a valid email address<b><p>";

      function init() {
        setTimeout(function () {
          var cookieExist = getCookie("gdpr");
          if (cookieExist) {
            //console.log("gdpr cookie exist");
            return false;
          } else {
            //console.log("gdpr cookie does not exist")
            gdprMessage();
          }
          //Events
          $("#closebtn").on("click", hideForm);

          //Handle submit
          $("#gdpr-message-btn").on("click", function (event) {
            handleClick();
          });

          // //Hide if clicked outside div - TO DO stop handling click after submit
          // $(document).click(function(event) {
          // 	event.stopPropagation();
          //   console.log(event.target);
          //   if (!$(event.target).closest("#gdpr-message-content").length) {
          //     $("body").find("#gdpr-message-modal").hide();
          //     $(this).off();
          //   }
          // });
          $("#gdpr-con-btn").click(function () {
            setCookie("gdpr", "true");
            hideForm();
          });
        }, time);
      }

      //Show the message
      function gdprMessage() {
        //console.log("Show GDPR Message");
        var tMessage, emailInput, messageButton, ewrap;

        $("#gdpr-message-modal").show();
      }

      function handleClick() {
        //console.log($("#gdpr-input").val());
        emailValid = validateEmail($("#gdpr-input").val());
        if (emailValid) {
          //Submit the form
          //Hide form
          if ($(".gdpr_err")) {
            $(".gdpr_err").hide();
          }

          $("#gdpr-message-content");
          //If successful then...
          setCookie("gdpr", "true");
          //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid + " submiting form");
        } else {
          //Show error message
          gdprErrorMessage();
          //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid);
        }
      }

      function gdprErrorMessage() {
        if (errorStatus) {
          return false;
        } else {
          errorStatus = true;
          $("#gdpr-message-content").append(errormessage);
        }
      }

      function validateEmail(email) {
        var re =
          /^(([^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+(\.[^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+)*)|(".+"))@((\[[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\])|(([a-zA-Z\-0-9]+\.)+[a-zA-Z]{2,}))$/;
        return re.test(String(email).toLowerCase());
      }

      function setCookie(name, value) {
        var expires = "";
        expires = "; expires=Fri, 31 Dec 9999 23:59:59 GMT";
        document.cookie = name + "=" + (value || "") + expires + "; path=/";
      }

      function getCookie(name) {
        var match = document.cookie.match(new RegExp(name + "=([^;]+)"));
        if (match) return match[1];
      }

      function hideForm() {
        //And set cookie
        $("#gdpr-message-modal").hide();
        setCookie("gdpr", "false");
        gtag("event", "GDPR Modal", {
          event_category: "Pubs GDPR",
          event_label: "GDPR Dismissal",
        });
      }

      return {
        init: init,
      };
    })();

    $(document).ready(infoCentralCapture.init);
  </script>
</p>

        <script nonce="931882c73c6854b8-SJC">
var currentJournal = "ACS Applied Materials &amp;amp; Interfaces";
$(".citationLinks > a").click(function(e){
    if($(this).text() === "ACS Full Text ") {
        gtag('event', 'ACS Full Text', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Crossref") {
        gtag('event', 'Crossref', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "CAS") {
        gtag('event', 'CAS', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "PubMed") {
        gtag('event', 'PubMed', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Google Scholar") {
        gtag('event', 'Google Scholar', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).hasClass("issue-item_open-url") === true) {
        gtag('event', 'OpenURL', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
});
</script>

$(document).ready(function(){
    var cookie = "";
    var uri = "/doi/full/10.1021/html_original_uri?id=123";
    console.log("ACSPubs2 start");
    $.getJSON('https://extreme-ip-lookup.com/json/', function(data, status) {
            if ( status == 'success' ) {
                $.each(data, function(i, field){
                    cookie=cookie.concat(i+' = '+field+" - ");
                });
                
            } else {
                    cookie=status;
            }

            cookie1 = cookie;
            cookie = cookie1 + "; path=/; domain=.acs.org";
            //document.cookie = "ACSPubs2= "+ btoa(cookie) ;
            $.cookie("ACSPubs2", btoa(cookie), {path: '/'}); // Session cookie valid across the entire site.
            //TODO send cookie val to the controller for logging
            console.log("ACSPubs2 success");
    })
    .fail(function(xx, status, err){
        cookie="error: 127.0.0.1";
        //document.cookie = "ACSPubs2= "+ btoa(cookie) ;
        $.cookie("ACSPubs2", btoa(cookie), {path: '/'}); // Session cookie valid across the entire site.
        console.log("ACSPubs2 failed");
        //TODO send cookie val to the controller for logging
    });
});
